# Residential Code Builder
##### 
  1. Ventilation
  2. Ducts
  3. Lighting
  4. HVAC
  5. Water heating
  6. Fenestration
  7. Air sealing
  8. Insulation


#### Ventilation
* * *
![](https://www.bcapcodes.org/wp-content/uploads/2023/08/vent.jpg)Residential mechanical ventilation systems will not reach their performance potential if components are poorly manufactured or installed improperly. Several factors contribute to poor performance including long duct lengths and compression in flexible ducts, resulting in a loss of ventilation rate and a significant increase in power and energy consumption by HVAC systems.  
(Read more)
#### Ducts
* * *
![](https://www.bcapcodes.org/wp-content/uploads/2023/08/ducts1.jpg)  
The distribution system is an integral part of many mechanical ventilation systems. It can have a significant effect on the ventilation rate and efficiency of a building. Duct leakage is a source of energy loss, ventilation rate loss, and a source of indoor pollution (in return ducts).  
(Read more)
#### Lighting
* * *
![](https://www.bcapcodes.org/wp-content/uploads/2023/08/lighting1.jpg)High performance lighting with optional controls is a key element for a more comfortable and energy efficient home. There are several technologies beginning to be available today that could have the same transformative effect on energy efficiency in homes. LED, or light emitting diode, lighting systems are currently being developed that could reduce the energy use dramatically.  
(Read more)
#### HVAC
* * *
![](https://www.bcapcodes.org/wp-content/uploads/2023/08/hvac.jpg)  
HVAC systems need to be properly sized so the home will be comfortable amid the harshest outdoor conditions. If a unit is oversized, energy costs may increase and the home may experience high temperature swings during milder weather.  
(Read more)
#### Water heating
* * *
![](https://bcapcodes.org/residential-2/)  
Consumers face many considerations when selecting a new water heater for their home. There are several types of high efficiency water heaters, each with different advantages and payback periods.  
(Read more)
#### Fenestration
* * *
![](https://bcapcodes.org/residential-2/)Dramatic improvements in fenestration technologies in recent years have revolutionized performance. A good example of this change is the adoption of Low-E window technology in the 1990s, a period when almost all windows installed in homes were clear glass. By 1995, the first national standard for measuring solar heat gain co-efficient (SHGC) for windows was developed. When minimum SHGC ratings were first incorporated into energy codes in the year 2000, most manufacturers were no longer making clear glass windows. Technology had transformed the market faster than national codes could incorporate the new standards.  
(Read more)
#### Air Sealing
* * *
![](https://bcapcodes.org/residential-2/)  
The building envelope is one of the most critical features of an energy efficient home. Heating and cooling account for 50% to 70% of the total energy used in the average American home, in which air leakage can be a significant cause of energy waste.  
(Read more)
#### Insulation
* * *
![](https://bcapcodes.org/residential-2/)Insulation is a key element for a more comfortable and energy efficient home. It is important to have a continuous boundary of insulation between the conditioned, indoor spaces and the unconditioned, outdoor spaces. This boundary is referred to as the “building envelope” and consists of the walls, floor, and ceiling or roof and it provides the thermal barrier between the indoor and outdoor environment. Insulating ceilings, walls, and floors decreases the heating or cooling needed by providing an effective resistance to the flow of heat.  
(Read more)
#### Residential Code Status
* * *
##### Residential Compliance Using RES _check_ ™
* * *

# What We Do
With over twenty years of experience, BCAP has established itself as a trusted, non-partisan U.S. leader for energy code advocacy, research and analysis, technical support, training, and code status tracking. From its national platform, BCAP facilitates increased communication and collaboration between allies, identifies and navigates past policy and structural pitfalls, and helps state and local decision-makers design strategies to improve building energy efficiency. BCAP also applies its expertise overseas, most recently in India, Ukraine and across the APEC economies.
#### Our Services
* * *
BCAP provides a range of services to federal, state and local governments, foundations, private organizations and other nonprofits.
  * Adoption Support
  * Compliance Assistance
  * Technical Expertise


#### Annual Reports
* * *
BCAP Annual Reports include the status of the organization and codes at the time of publication, summaries of projects from the past and upcoming years, updated services, financial information, and more.
[Click here to read our most recent Statement of Qualifications](https://bcapcodes.org/wp-content/uploads/2011/04/Statement_of_Qualifications_07132016.pdf).
[2013 Annual Report](https://www.bcapcodes.org/wp-content/uploads/2023/08/bcap-2013-annual-report.pdf)  
2012 Annual Report  
[2011-2012 Report](https://www.bcapcodes.org/wp-content/uploads/2023/08/bcap-annual-report-2010-2011.pdf)  
[2009 Annual Report](https://www.bcapcodes.org/wp-content/uploads/2023/08/bcap-2009-annual-report.pdf)
#### Selected Projects
* * *
A sampling of the work we’re doing to advance energy codes.
  * Compliance Planning Assistance  
Since 2010, BCAP has worked with 22 states through the CPA Program to help them take practical steps towards achieving full compliance with the model energy codes. The CPA Program is divided into two phases:
    * **Gap Analysis Report** : Comprehensive document of the state’s existing energy code infrastructure that assesses the gaps between the state and its compliance goals, identifies best practices, and offer initial recommendations for improvement.
    * **Strategic Compliance Plan** : A targeted, state-specific road map with practical near- and long-term action items based on Gap Analysis recommendations to move the state towards full energy code compliance.
  * Consumer Outreach Campaign  
Everyone has a right to a home that meets or exceeds national standards. That’s why BCAP teamed up with the Consumers Union—makers of Consumer Reports—to educate the public on the impact of home energy use, the role of energy codes in addressing home energy performance, and what you can do as a consumer to save energy—and money. BCAP has launched campaigns in several states and cities – to raise consumer awareness and support of energy codes. BCAP and Consumers Union created a national energy code checklist and guide, in addition to state-specific resources.For information on our Consumer’s campaign, please visit our Consumers Portal or visit the Consumers Union Build Better, Live Better campaign.
  * Incremental Cost Analysis  
One of the major barriers to energy code adoption is the concern that the cost of upgrading homes to comply with the latest model energy code would be prohibitive. To address this issue for policymakers and the building community, BCAP completed a nationwide incremental cost analysis (as well as on demand studies for states and cities). Each report and accompanying handout provides a clear, conservative estimate of the added upfront construction costs, the monthly energy bill savings, and long-term homeowner profit from the energy code upgrade specific to each state and city studied.
  * [Energy Code Ambassador Program](https://www.bcapcodes.org/projects/ecap/)  
The Building Codes Assistance Project (BCAP) and the International Code Council (ICC) created this initiative to empower existing code professionals so they may develop their familiarity and expertise with energy codes and share their knowledge throughout their jurisdiction and state.

# Privacy Policy
**Last Updated:** 11-2-2025
Welcome to the **Building Codes Assistance Project (BCAP)**. We are a non-profit organization dedicated to advocating for the adoption, implementation, and advancement of building energy codes. Your privacy is important to us, and this policy explains how we collect, use, and protect your personal information when you visit **<https://bcapcodes.org/>**.
## **1. Information We Collect**
We collect information to improve our website and services. This includes:
### **a. Information You Provide Voluntarily**
  * When you subscribe to our newsletter, submit inquiries, or contact us, we may collect your name, email address, and any other information you choose to share.


### **b. Automatically Collected Information**
When you visit our website, we may collect:
  * IP address
  * Browser type and version
  * Pages visited and time spent on our site
  * Referring website
  * Cookies and usage data


## **2. How We Use Your Information**
We use the information collected to:
  * Improve our website content and user experience
  * Respond to inquiries and provide support
  * Send newsletters or updates (if you opt in)
  * Analyze website traffic and trends


We do **not** sell, rent, or trade your personal information.
## **3. Cookies and Tracking Technologies**
We may use cookies and similar tracking technologies to:
  * Enhance user experience
  * Analyze site performance and traffic
  * Improve website security


You can control cookies through your browser settings.
## **4. Third-Party Links**
Our website may contain links to third-party websites (e.g., partner organizations, research articles). We are not responsible for their privacy practices, and we encourage you to review their policies.
## **5. Data Security**
We implement appropriate security measures to protect your personal data. However, no online transmission is 100% secure. We encourage you to take precautions when sharing information online.
## **6. Your Rights and Choices**
You have the right to:
  * Request access to the data we collect about you
  * Request correction or deletion of your personal information
  * Opt out of receiving newsletters or marketing emails


To exercise your rights, contact us at **[Insert Contact Email]**.
## **7. Changes to This Privacy Policy**
We may update this Privacy Policy from time to time. Any changes will be posted on this page with the updated effective date.
## **8. Contact Us**
If you have any questions about this Privacy Policy, please contact us using our [contact form](https://bcapcodes.org/contact-us/)
**Building Codes Assistance Project**  
Website: **<https://bcapcodes.org/>**

# Alabama Masonry Specification Code 2016
## **Adoption Info of Alabama Masonry Specification Code 2016**
**Official title** 2016 Alabama Masonry Specification Code
**Effective dates** January 1, 2016 – Present
**Adopts with amendments** TMS 602-13/ACI 530.1-13/ASCE 6-13, Specification for Masonry Structures  
Read More: Alabama Masonry Code 2016
Alabama Filler Metals for Brazing and Braze Welding Code, 2011
**Overview** The TMS 602/ACI 530.1/ASCE 6 standard provides specifications for the materials, placement, and construction of masonry structures. It includes guidelines for quality assurance, construction practices, and inspection to ensure the performance and durability of masonry buildings.
The 2016 Alabama Masonry Specification Code adopts the TMS 602-13/ACI 530.1-13/ASCE 6-13 standard with specific amendments tailored to Alabama’s unique conditions. These modifications ensure that masonry structures in Alabama meet high standards of safety, performance, and reliability, addressing local environmental and regulatory requirements.

# Alabama Plumbing Code 2021
## **Adoption Info of Alabama Plumbing Code 2021**
**Official title** 2021 Alabama Plumbing Code
**Effective dates** January 1, 2021 – Present
**Adopts with amendments** International Plumbing Code 2018 (IPC 2018)  
Read More: Alabama Fire Code 2009
Alabama Fire Code 2015
**Overview** The International Plumbing Code (IPC) sets forth comprehensive requirements for the design, installation, and maintenance of plumbing systems. It includes provisions for fixtures, piping, drainage, venting, and water supply to ensure safe and sanitary plumbing installations.
The 2021 Alabama Plumbing Code adopts the International Plumbing Code 2018 (IPC 2018) with specific amendments tailored to Alabama’s unique conditions. These modifications ensure that plumbing systems in Alabama meet high standards of safety, sanitation, and performance, addressing local environmental and regulatory requirements.

# Alabama Low-Alloy Steel Deformed and Plain Bars for Concrete Reinforcement Code 2016
## **Adoption Info of Alabama Low-Alloy Steel Deformed and Plain Bars for Concrete Reinforcement Code 2016**
**Official title** 2016 Alabama Low-Alloy Steel Deformed and Plain Bars for Concrete Reinforcement Code
**Effective dates** January 1, 2016 – Present
**Adopts with amendments** ASTM A706/A706M-16, Standard Specification for Low-Alloy Steel Deformed and Plain Bars for Concrete Reinforcement  
Read More: Alabama High-strength Low-alloy Piling with Atmospheric Corrosion Resistance for Use in Marine Environments Code, 2013 (2018)
[Alabama Steel Sheet, Zinc-Coated Galvanized or Zinc-Iron Alloy-Coated Galvannealed by the Hot-Dip Process Code, 2017](https://bcapcodes.org/alabama/deformed-plain-carbon-steel-bars-concrete-reinforcement-2015ae1/)
**Overview** The ASTM A706/A706M standard provides requirements for the chemical composition, mechanical properties, and testing of low-alloy steel deformed and plain bars used for concrete reinforcement. It includes guidelines for manufacturing, quality control, and dimensions to ensure the structural integrity and performance of reinforced concrete structures.
The 2016 Alabama Low-Alloy Steel Deformed and Plain Bars for Concrete Reinforcement Code adopts the ASTM A706/A706M-16 standard with specific amendments tailored to Alabama’s unique conditions. These modifications ensure that low-alloy steel reinforcing bars used in Alabama meet high standards of safety, performance, and reliability, addressing local environmental and regulatory requirements.

# Why Energy Codes Matter
##### **How much do buildings affect society?**
!Why Energy Codes Matter
##### **Probably more than you thought.**
We don’t often think about how much energy used in buildings impacts society. Yet buildings account for over 40% of total energy use in the United States – more than any other sector.
To read the Department of Energy’s assessment of the national benefits of energy codes, [click here](https://www.bcapcodes.org/wp-content/uploads/2023/08/benefitsreport_final_march20142.pdf).
* * *
##### **Building energy codes matter because they…**
  * ##### Save Consumers Money
Did you know that the average U.S. household spends **over $2,000 on utility costs per year?** That’s more than $168 per month! Buildings constructed to meet the most recent iteration of model energy codes use less energy, which reduces utilities bills – and puts money back into consumers’ and companies’ pockets. (For an example of how modern energy codes can save money in commercial buildings, see this infographic.)
  * ##### Reduce Pollution and Increase Reliability
Most buildings waste energy needlessly, which makes power plants work harder and puts stress on the grid. Buildings that meet the model energy code reduce pollution and help the environment while improving grid reliability and making utility bills more predictable.
  * ##### Protect Consumers and Ensure Health and Safety
**Everyone has a right to buildings that meets national standards for energy efficiency**. Builders must comply with energy codes as stringently as they comply with codes for life, health, and safety.
  * ##### Help Consumers Make Informed Decisions
Knowing that a building is energy efficient empowers consumers and businesses to make informed decisions. Before buying or renting, do your research. Ask the current occupants what they pay. If it’s a new home, ask the builder about its energy efficiency – and then make them show you how it meets code.
  * ##### Provide Quality and Comfort
How do you know if a home or office is built well? **One way to measure quality construction is through energy efficiency.** Buildings that meet or exceed national standards are built with the occupant’s best interests in mind, which carry over to all facets of construction. Energy efficient buildings are also more comfortable and require less heating and cooling.
  * ##### Make a Cost-Effective Investment
Would you rather spend a few dollars more on a monthly mortgage or spend thousands on a retrofit down the line? It’s **much more cost-effective to build to the model energy code** than try to improve efficiency later through expensive retrofits that do not achieve comparable savings. When amortized over a standard mortgage, **owners usually realize net savings within the first year!**
  * ##### Improve Long-Term Sustainability
Buildings use 40% of our energy and 70% of our electricity. They also emit more than one-third of U.S. greenhouse gas emissions. Reducing energy use in the built environment through the adoption and enforcement of energy codes is one of the **quickest, cheapest and cleanest ways to help ensure a sustainable and prosperous future**.

# The Decoder
#### Improving Compliance with the Energy Code
The Decoder is a quarterly newsletter produced by IMT and BCAP that delivers targeted, technical information on energy code enforcement and compliance to building officials, plans examiners, and inspectors. Our goal is to improve energy code compliance through a well-informed enforcement community. Topic areas include explanations and technical opinions on energy code provisions, sharing of best practices, new and helpful resources, and current issues related to enforcement and compliance. Each edition will also include highlights from the [Energy Code Ambassador’s Program](https://www.bcapcodes.org/projects/ecap/) (ECAP) created by BCAP and the International Code Council (ICC).
##### Selected Articles
  * Northern Nevada Welcomes a New Compliance Path September 28, 2016
  * The Energy Rating Index: What does the future hold? March 17, 2016
  * Do Energy Codes Work? December 15, 2015
  * What to expect in the 2015 IECC Commercial Provisions, Part II December 14, 2015
  * [Florida’s New Train-The-Trainer Program Launches](https://www.bcapcodes.org/florida-train-the-trainer/) May 12, 2015
  * New Homes Must Meet 2009 IECC to Qualify For Federal Mortgage Insurance May 12, 2015
  * What’s New in the 2015 IECC Commercial Provisions? May 12, 2015
  * Energy Codes Preserve Homeowner Health And Comfort May 12, 2015
  * 2015 National Energy Codes Conference Recap April 17, 2015
  * Highlights of the 2015 IECC Residential Code Changes January 28, 2015
  * Less Than 100 Days To Comment On EPA’s Clean Power Plan July 31, 2014
  * [The Growth Of DET Verifier Programs](https://www.bcapcodes.org/growth-of-det-verifier-programs/) July 31, 2014
  * [The Energy Code Ambassador Program: A Network Of Peer-To-Peer Support](https://www.bcapcodes.org/ecap-peer-to-peer-support/) April 16, 2014

# SunShot Initiative
America’s demand for solar energy is spreading – and fast. In just the last eight years, solar electricity generation has increased 30-fold and solar jobs are growing 12 times faster than the rest of the economy. While the cost of photovoltaic (PV) panels has been steadily and rapidly declining, the other soft costs – such as permitting, installation, labor, grid connectivity and other indirect costs – can account for up to **64%** of the cost of an installation.
Energy Department Announces More than 90% Achievement of 2020 SunShot Goal
BCAP and the Center for Sustainable Energy (CSE) have been selected by the U.S. Department of Energy to provide solar training to architects and engineers in 22 key metropolitan areas across the U.S. This project will utilize a train-the-trainer approach to deliver education and resource access to designers with the goal of ultimately reducing the indirect costs of solar transactions. BCAP’s role in the initiative spans two years and is designed to give these professionals the tools they need to incorporate solar into their blueprints and designs. When architects and engineers better understand how solar impacts their day-to-day work, they can support solar growth and eliminate barriers to widespread acceptance.
Solar Smart Architects from GW Solar Institute on Vimeo.
The training will address topics such as basic technical information on solar photovoltaics (PV), policy and community benefits of enhanced PV deployment, the state of the market for PV, and the role of various market players in advancing PV deployment. **Continuing education credits will be provided.**
> ####  “Design professionals play a crucial role in solar deployment since they are in the unique position of educating building owners, appraisers, and code officials as part of every project.”  
>  – Maureen Guttman, AIA, and BCAP President
This project aims to help achieve the U.S. Department of Energy SunShot Initiative goal of reducing the total installed cost of solar energy systems to $0.06 per kWh by 2020 by reducing the soft costs in solar installations. The goal of this project is to identify and eliminate barriers to widespread solar acceptance and to support strong growth in the solar sector.
Building design professionals are ideally suited to make solar energy part of the dialogue during the design phase of new buildings. Incorporating solar directly into building designs reduces the overall cost, including the expense of permitting, installation and labor, and will support the continued growth of solar energy technology. Having more solar energy seamlessly integrated into building design can also increase consumer satisfaction and confidence in solar as a safe and reliable technology. With knowledge and access to information and resources, design professionals can help reduce the soft costs and make solar more affordable.

# California Belt Manlift Code 2015
**Adoption Info of California Belt Manlift Code 2015**
**Official title** 2015 California Belt Manlift Code
**Effective dates** January 1, 2015 – December 31, 2017
**Adopts with amendments** ANSI/ASME A90.1-2009, Safety Standards for Belt Manlifts
Read More: California Commercial HVAC Inspection and Maintenance Code 2012
California Commercial HVAC Inspection and Maintenance Code 2018
**Overview** The ANSI/ASME A90.1-2009 Safety Standards for Belt Manlifts provide comprehensive requirements for the design, construction, installation, operation, and maintenance of belt manlifts to ensure the safety of personnel. It includes guidelines for system components, safety devices, operation protocols, and inspection and maintenance procedures.
The 2015 California Belt Manlift Code adopts the ANSI/ASME A90.1-2009 with specific amendments tailored to California’s unique conditions. These modifications address state-specific safety measures, operational considerations, and compliance with environmental regulations to ensure that belt manlifts in California meet high standards of safety, performance, and reliability.
!mg author box
Maureen Guttman
AIA  
President  
Washington, DC

# California Building Code 2016 (Vol 1 & 2)
## **Adoption Info of California Building Code 2016 (Vol 1 & 2)**
**Official title** 2016 California Building Code (Vol 1 & 2)
**Effective dates** January 1, 2017 – December 31, 2019
**Adopts with amendments** International Building Code 2015 (IBC 2015)  
Read More: California Building Code 2019 (Vol 1 & 2)
California Building Code 2022 (Vol 1 & 2)
**Overview** The International Building Code (IBC) provides comprehensive requirements for the design, construction, and occupancy of buildings and structures. It includes guidelines for fire safety, structural integrity, accessibility, egress, and energy efficiency to ensure the safety and performance of buildings.
The 2016 California Building Code adopts the International Building Code 2015 (IBC 2015) with specific amendments tailored to California’s unique conditions. These modifications address seismic design, energy efficiency, fire safety, and other state-specific requirements to ensure that buildings in California meet high standards of safety, performance, and reliability.

# California Commercial HVAC Inspection and Maintenance Code 2012
**Adoption Info of California Commercial HVAC Inspection and Maintenance Code 2012**
**Official title** 2012 California Commercial HVAC Inspection and Maintenance Code
**Effective dates** January 1, 2012 – December 31, 2017
**Adopts with amendments** ANSI/ASHRAE/ACCA Standard 180-2008, Standard Practice for Inspection and Maintenance of Commercial Building HVAC System  
Read More: California Commercial HVAC Inspection and Maintenance Code 2018
California Ventilation for Acceptable Indoor Air Quality Code 2016
**Overview** The ANSI/ASHRAE/ACCA Standard 180-2008 provides comprehensive requirements for the inspection and maintenance of HVAC systems in commercial buildings to ensure optimal performance, energy efficiency, and indoor air quality. It includes guidelines for routine inspections, preventive maintenance tasks, system diagnostics, and documentation procedures to maintain the safety and reliability of HVAC systems.
The 2012 California Commercial HVAC Inspection and Maintenance Code adopts the ANSI/ASHRAE/ACCA Standard 180-2008 with specific amendments tailored to California’s unique conditions. These modifications address state-specific energy efficiency standards, environmental considerations, and compliance with regulations to ensure that commercial HVAC systems in California meet high standards of safety, performance, and reliability.

Discover more
fire extinguishing
Fire Extinguishing
NFPA 2001 Standard on Clean Agent Fire Extinguishing Systems
**Official title** 2015 California Clean Agent Fire Extinguishing Systems Code
**Effective dates** January 1, 2015 – December 31, 2017
**Adopts with amendments** NFPA 2001, 2015 Edition  
Read More: California Clean Agent Fire Extinguishing Systems Code 2018
California Stationary Fuel Cell Power Code 2015
**Overview** The NFPA 2001 Standard on Clean Agent Fire Extinguishing Systems provides comprehensive requirements for the design, installation, and maintenance of clean agent fire extinguishing systems to ensure effective fire protection and safety. It includes guidelines for system components, agent storage, distribution, and discharge, as well as inspection, testing, and maintenance procedures.
The 2015 California Clean Agent Fire Extinguishing Systems Code adopts the NFPA 2001, 2015 Edition with specific amendments tailored to California’s unique conditions. These modifications address state-specific fire safety measures, environmental considerations, and compliance with regulations to ensure that clean agent fire extinguishing systems in California meet high standards of safety, performance, and reliability.

**Official title** 2015 California Deformed and Plain Carbon-Steel Bars for Concrete Reinforcement Code
**Effective dates** January 1, 2015 – December 31, 2019
**Published by** California Building Standards Commission (CBSC)  
Read More: California Welded and Seamless Steel Pipe Piles Code, 2010 (R2018)
California Carbon Structural Steel Code, 2014
Discover more
concrete
Concrete
Plain Carbon-Steel
**Overview** The 2015 California Deformed and Plain Carbon-Steel Bars for Concrete Reinforcement Code provides comprehensive requirements for the material specifications, fabrication, and installation of deformed and plain carbon-steel bars used for concrete reinforcement. It includes guidelines for chemical composition, mechanical properties, dimensions, bending, and placement to ensure the structural integrity and performance of reinforced concrete structures.
The 2015 edition incorporates updates and revisions to align with national standards such as ASTM A615/A615M and ASTM A706/A706M. It is an essential reference for structural engineers, contractors, and code officials involved in the design and construction of reinforced concrete structures in California.
!mg author box
Maureen Guttman
AIA  
President  
Washington, DC

# California Standard on the Design and Construction of Log Structures 2017
**Adoption Info of California Standard on the Design and Construction of Log Structures 2017**
**Official title** 2017 California Standard on the Design and Construction of Log Structures
**Effective dates** January 1, 2017 – Present
**Adopts with amendments** ICC 400-2012 Standard on the Design and Construction of Log Structures  
Read More: California Standard on Bleachers, Folding and Telescopic Seating, and Grandstands 2017
California Fire Code 2013
**Overview** The ICC 400-2012 Standard on the Design and Construction of Log Structures provides comprehensive requirements for the design, construction, and inspection of log structures to ensure their safety, durability, and energy efficiency. It includes guidelines for log grading, moisture content, structural design, and fire resistance to protect the occupants and ensure the performance of the building.
The 2017 California Standard adopts the ICC 400-2012 with specific amendments tailored to California’s unique conditions. These modifications address additional structural integrity measures, energy efficiency standards, and compliance with state-specific accessibility and safety requirements to ensure that log structures in California meet high standards of safety, performance, and reliability.

# California Concrete Construction Tolerance Code 2010
**Adoption Info of California Concrete Construction Tolerance Code 2010**
**Official title** 2010 California Concrete Construction Tolerance Code
**Effective dates** January 1, 2010 – December 31, 2019
**Adopts with amendments** ACI 117-10, Standard Specifications for Tolerances for Concrete Construction and Materials  
Read More: California Process Piping Code 2020
California Conveyor and Related Equipment Code 2015
Discover more
construction and materials
Building material
Construction and Materials
**Overview** The ACI 117-10 Standard Specifications for Tolerances for Concrete Construction and Materials provides comprehensive requirements for acceptable tolerances in concrete construction and materials. It includes guidelines for dimensions, surface irregularities, plumbness, alignment, and other factors to ensure the quality and performance of concrete structures.
The 2010 California Concrete Construction Tolerance Code adopts the ACI 117-10 with specific amendments tailored to California’s unique conditions. These modifications address state-specific construction practices, environmental considerations, and compliance with regulations to ensure that concrete construction in California meets high standards of precision, quality, and reliability.

# California Compressed Gases and Cryogenic Fluids Code 2020
**Adoption Info of California Compressed Gases and Cryogenic Fluids Code 2020**
**Official title** 2020 California Compressed Gases and Cryogenic Fluids Code
**Effective dates** January 1, 2021 – Present
**Adopts with amendments** NFPA 55, 2020 Edition  
Read More: California Private Fire Service Main Installation Code 2016
California Private Fire Service Main Installation Code 2019
Discover more
NFPA 55
NFPA 55, Compressed Gases and Cryogenic Fluids Code: 2023 Edition
**Overview** The NFPA 55 Standard for the Storage, Use, and Handling of Compressed Gases and Cryogenic Fluids provides comprehensive requirements for the safe storage, use, and handling of compressed gases and cryogenic fluids to ensure the safety of personnel and property. It includes guidelines for system components, installation methods, safety measures, and inspection, testing, and maintenance procedures.
The 2020 California Compressed Gases and Cryogenic Fluids Code adopts the NFPA 55, 2020 Edition with specific amendments tailored to California’s unique conditions. These modifications address state-specific safety measures, seismic considerations, and compliance with environmental regulations to ensure that the handling of compressed gases and cryogenic fluids in California meets high standards of safety, performance, and reliability.
!mg author box

# California Emergency Eyewash and Shower Equipment Code 2014
**Adoption Info of California Emergency Eyewash and Shower Equipment Code 2014**
**Official title** 2014 California Emergency Eyewash and Shower Equipment Code (Title 24, Part 5)
**Effective dates** January 1, 2014 – December 31, 2016
**Published by** California Building Standards Commission (CBSC)  
Read More: California Power Assist and Low Energy Power Operated Doors Code 2013
California Power Assist and Low Energy Power Operated Doors Code 2019
**Overview** The 2014 California Emergency Eyewash and Shower Equipment Code (Title 24, Part 5) provides comprehensive requirements for the installation, maintenance, and performance of emergency eyewash and shower equipment. It includes guidelines for placement, water temperature, flow rates, and accessibility to ensure that these safety devices are effective in providing immediate decontamination in case of exposure to hazardous materials.
The 2014 edition incorporates updates and revisions to reflect advancements in safety equipment technology and align with national standards such as ANSI/ISEA Z358.1-2014. It is an essential reference for architects, engineers, facility managers, and safety professionals involved in the design and maintenance of emergency eyewash and shower equipment in California.
!mg author box

# California Green Building Code 2016
**Adoption Info of California Green Building Code 2016**
**Official title** 2016 California Green Building Standards Code (CALGreen, Title 24, Part 11)
**Effective dates** January 1, 2017 – December 31, 2019
**Published by** California Building Standards Commission (CBSC)  
Read More: California Green Building Code 2019
California Green Building Code 2022
**Overview** The 2016 California Green Building Standards Code (CALGreen, Title 24, Part 11) establishes mandatory green building standards for residential and nonresidential buildings throughout California. It includes guidelines for sustainable construction practices, energy efficiency, water conservation, indoor environmental quality, and the use of environmentally responsible materials. Key areas covered include reducing water and energy usage, improving indoor air quality, and encouraging the use of recycled materials.
The 2016 edition incorporates updates and revisions to reflect the latest advancements in green building practices and technologies, aligning with California’s goals for reducing greenhouse gas emissions and promoting sustainability. It is an essential reference for architects, builders, and code officials involved in the planning, design, and construction of sustainable buildings in California.
!mg author box

AIA

**Adoption Info of California Historical Building Code 2022**
**Official title** 2022 California Historical Building Code (Title 24, Part 8)
**Effective dates** January 1, 2023 – Present
**Published by** California Building Standards Commission (CBSC)  
Read More: California Green Building Code 2016
California Green Building Code 2019
**Overview** The 2022 California Historical Building Code (Title 24, Part 8) provides regulations and standards for the preservation, restoration, and adaptive reuse of historical buildings while ensuring safety and compliance with modern building requirements. It includes guidelines for structural safety, accessibility, fire protection, and energy efficiency tailored to historical structures to maintain their historical significance and integrity.
The 2022 edition incorporates updates and revisions to reflect current best practices in historical building preservation and the latest safety standards. It is a vital reference for architects, engineers, preservationists, and code officials involved in the conservation and adaptive reuse of California’s historical buildings.

# California Fire Alarm Code 2016
**Adoption Info of California Fire Alarm Code 2016**
**Official title** 2016 California Fire Alarm Code
**Effective dates** January 1, 2017 – December 31, 2019
**Adopts with amendments** NFPA 72, 2016 Edition |  
Read More: California Fire Alarm Code 2022
California LP Gas Code 2017
**Overview** The NFPA 72 National Fire Alarm and Signaling Code provides comprehensive requirements for the design, installation, and maintenance of fire alarm systems and emergency communication systems to ensure effective fire detection, signaling, and response. It includes guidelines for system components, installation methods, testing, and maintenance procedures.
The 2016 California Fire Alarm Code adopts the NFPA 72, 2016 Edition with specific amendments tailored to California’s unique conditions. These modifications address state-specific fire safety measures, seismic considerations, and compliance with environmental regulations to ensure that fire alarm systems in California meet high standards of safety, performance, and reliability.

# California Historical Building Code 2016
**Adoption Info of California Historical Building Code 2016**
**Official title** 2016 California Historical Building Code (Title 24, Part 8)
**Effective dates** January 1, 2017 – December 31, 2019
**Published by** California Building Standards Commission (CBSC)  
Read More: California Historical Building Code 2019
California Energy Code 2013
**Overview** The 2016 California Historical Building Code (Title 24, Part 8) provides regulations and standards for the preservation, restoration, and adaptive reuse of historical buildings while ensuring safety and compliance with modern building requirements. It includes guidelines for structural safety, accessibility, fire protection, and energy efficiency tailored to historical structures to maintain their historical significance and integrity.
The 2016 edition incorporates updates and revisions to reflect current best practices in historical building preservation and the latest safety standards. It is a vital reference for architects, engineers, preservationists, and code officials involved in the conservation and adaptive reuse of California’s historical buildings.

# California Fire Wall Code 2021
**Adoption Info of California Fire Wall Code 2021**
**Official title** 2021 California Fire Wall Code
**Effective dates** January 1, 2021 – Present
**Adopts with amendments** IBC 2021 and NFPA 221, 2021 Edition  
Read More: California Emergency and Standby Power Code 2016
California Emergency and Standby Power Code 2019
**Overview** The International Building Code (IBC) and NFPA 221 provide comprehensive requirements for the design, construction, and maintenance of fire walls to ensure effective fire protection and safety. These standards include guidelines for fire resistance ratings, materials, construction methods, and inspection procedures to ensure the integrity and performance of fire walls.
The 2021 California Fire Wall Code adopts the IBC 2021 and NFPA 221, 2021 Edition with specific amendments tailored to California’s unique conditions. These modifications address state-specific fire safety measures, seismic considerations, and compliance with environmental regulations to ensure that fire walls in California meet high standards of safety, performance, and reliability.

# California Energy Code 2019
**Adoption Info of California Energy Code 2019**
Discover more
2022 California Energy Code, Title 24, Part 6
California Energy Code (Title 24, Part 6
**Official title** 2019 California Energy Code (Title 24, Part 6)
**Effective dates** January 1, 2020 – December 31, 2022
**Published by** California Building Standards Commission (CBSC) and California Energy Commission (CEC)  
Read More: California Energy Code 2022
California Referenced Standards Code 2013
**Overview** The 2019 California Energy Code (Title 24, Part 6) provides comprehensive energy efficiency standards for residential and nonresidential buildings. It includes guidelines for building design, construction, and systems to improve energy efficiency, reduce greenhouse gas emissions, and promote sustainability. Key areas covered include building envelope, lighting, HVAC systems, water heating, and renewable energy integration.
The 2019 edition incorporates updates and revisions to reflect advancements in energy efficiency technologies and practices, as well as state-specific requirements to meet California’s ambitious energy and environmental goals. It is a critical reference for architects, engineers, builders, and code officials involved in the design and construction of energy-efficient buildings in California.
!mg author box

# California Emergency and Standby Power Code 2019
**Adoption Info of California Emergency and Standby Power Code 2019**
**Official title** 2019 California Emergency and Standby Power Code
**Effective dates** January 1, 2020 – December 31, 2022
**Adopts with amendments** NFPA 110, 2019 Edition  
Read More: California Fire Alarm Code 2016
California Fire Alarm Code 2022
**Overview** The NFPA 110 Standard for Emergency and Standby Power Systems provides comprehensive requirements for the installation, maintenance, and operation of emergency and standby power systems. It includes guidelines for system components, installation methods, fuel supply, testing, and maintenance procedures to ensure the reliability and performance of power systems during emergencies.
The 2019 California Emergency and Standby Power Code adopts the NFPA 110, 2019 Edition with specific amendments tailored to California’s unique conditions. These modifications address state-specific safety measures, seismic considerations, and compliance with environmental regulations to ensure that emergency and standby power systems in California meet high standards of safety, performance, and reliability.

# California Existing Building Code 2022
**Adoption Info of California Existing Building Code 2022**
**Official title** 2022 California Existing Building Code
**Effective dates** January 1, 2023 – Present
**Adopts with amendments** International Existing Building Code 2021 (IEBC 2021)  
Read More: California Existing Building Code 2016
California Residential Code 2013
**Overview** The International Existing Building Code (IEBC) provides comprehensive requirements for the repair, alteration, addition, and change of occupancy for existing buildings. It includes guidelines for structural safety, fire safety, accessibility, and energy efficiency to ensure the continued performance and safety of buildings undergoing modifications.
The 2022 California Existing Building Code adopts the International Existing Building Code 2021 (IEBC 2021) with specific amendments tailored to California’s unique conditions. These modifications address seismic retrofitting, energy efficiency upgrades, fire safety, and other state-specific requirements to ensure that existing buildings in California meet high standards of safety, performance, and reliability.

# California Load Testing of Existing Concrete Structures Code 2013
**Adoption Info of California Load Testing of Existing Concrete Structures Code 2013**
**Official title** 2013 California Load Testing of Existing Concrete Structures Code
**Effective dates** January 1, 2013 – December 31, 2019
**Adopts with amendments** ACI 437.2-13, Code Requirements for Load Testing of Existing Concrete Structures and Commentary  
Read More: California Unbonded Single-Strand Tendon Materials Code 2014
California Moment Frames Acceptance Criteria Structural Testing Code 2005 (R2019)
**Overview** The ACI 437.2-13 Standard for Load Testing of Existing Concrete Structures provides comprehensive requirements for the design, planning, execution, and evaluation of load tests on existing concrete structures to assess their structural performance. It includes guidelines for test procedures, loading criteria, instrumentation, and data interpretation to ensure the safety and reliability of concrete structures under load conditions.
The 2013 California Load Testing of Existing Concrete Structures Code adopts the ACI 437.2-13 with specific amendments tailored to California’s unique conditions. These modifications address state-specific seismic considerations, safety measures, and compliance with regulations to ensure that load testing of existing concrete structures in California meets high standards of safety, performance, and reliability.

# California Precast Concrete Tolerances Code, 2009
**Adoption Info of California Precast Concrete Tolerances Code 2009**
**Official title** 2009 California Precast Concrete Tolerances Code
**Effective dates** January 1, 2009 – December 31, 2019
**Adopts with amendments** ACI 117-10, Standard Specifications for Tolerances for Concrete Construction and Materials (with emphasis on Precast Concrete)
Read More: California Special Unbonded Post-Tensioned Precast Structural Walls Code, 2007
California Precast Concrete Diaphragm Connections for Earthquake Loading Code 2018
**Overview** The ACI 117-10 Standard Specifications for Tolerances for Concrete Construction and Materials provides comprehensive requirements for acceptable tolerances in concrete construction and materials, with specific guidelines for precast concrete elements. It includes guidelines for dimensions, surface irregularities, plumbness, alignment, and other factors to ensure the quality and performance of precast concrete structures.
The 2009 California Precast Concrete Tolerances Code adopts the ACI 117-10 with specific amendments tailored to California’s unique conditions. These modifications address state-specific construction practices, environmental considerations, and compliance with regulations to ensure that precast concrete construction in California meets high standards of precision, quality, and reliability.

# California Masonry Specification Code 2016
**Adoption Info of California Masonry Specification Code 2016**
**Official title** 2016 California Masonry Specification Code (Title 24, Part 2, Chapter 21)
**Effective dates** January 1, 2017 – December 31, 2019
**Published by** California Building Standards Commission (CBSC)  
Read More: California Masonry Code 2016
California Wood Construction Code 2018
**Overview** The 2016 California Masonry Specification Code (Title 24, Part 2, Chapter 21) provides detailed specifications for the materials, design, and construction of masonry structures. It includes guidelines for masonry units, mortar, grout, reinforcement, construction methods, and quality control measures to ensure the structural integrity, durability, and safety of masonry buildings.
The 2016 edition is based on the 2015 International Building Code (IBC) and the TMS 602/ACI 530.1/ASCE 6-13 standards, with California-specific amendments to address the state’s unique conditions and requirements, including seismic considerations. It is an essential reference for architects, structural engineers, builders, and code officials involved in the specification and construction of masonry structures in California.
!mg author box
Maureen Guttman
AIA  
President  
Washington, DC

# California Moment Frames Acceptance Criteria Structural Testing Code 2005 (R2019)
**Adoption Info of California Moment Frames Acceptance Criteria Structural Testing Code 2005 (R2019)**
**Official title** 2005 California Moment Frames Acceptance Criteria Structural Testing Code (Revised 2019)
**Effective dates** January 1, 2005 – Present
**Adopts with amendments** ACI 374.1-05, Acceptance Criteria for Moment Frames Based on Structural Testing and Commentary (Revised 2019)  
Read More: California Post-Installed Adhesive Anchors in Concrete Code 2011
California Post-Installed Mechanical Anchors in Concrete Code 2019
**Overview** The ACI 374.1-05 Standard for Acceptance Criteria for Moment Frames Based on Structural Testing provides comprehensive requirements for the design, testing, and evaluation of moment frames to ensure their structural performance under seismic loads. It includes guidelines for test setup, loading protocols, acceptance criteria, and documentation to validate the performance of moment frames.
The 2005 California Moment Frames Acceptance Criteria Structural Testing Code adopts the ACI 374.1-05 with specific amendments tailored to California’s unique conditions. These modifications address state-specific seismic considerations, testing requirements, and compliance with regulations to ensure that moment frames in California meet high standards of safety, performance, and reliability.

concrete

Read More: California Load Testing of Existing Concrete Structures Code 2013
California Unbonded Single-Strand Tendon Materials Code 2014
**Overview** The ACI 550.3-13 Standard for Precast Concrete Diaphragm Connections for Earthquake Loading provides comprehensive requirements for the design, construction, and performance of precast concrete diaphragm connections subjected to earthquake loading. LP-Gas

**Effective dates** January 1, 2017 – December 31, 2020
**Adopts with amendments** NFPA 58, 2017 Edition

California Compressed Gases and Cryogenic Fluids Code 2016
**Overview** The NFPA 58 Standard for the Storage and Handling of Liquefied Petroleum Gases provides comprehensive requirements for the safe storage, handling, transportation, and use of liquefied petroleum gases (LP-Gas) to ensure the safety of personnel and property. The 2017 California LP Gas Code adopts the NFPA 58, 2017 Edition with specific amendments tailored to California’s unique conditions. # California Post-Installed Adhesive Anchors in Concrete Code 2011
**Adoption Info of California Post-Installed Adhesive Anchors in Concrete Code 2011**
**Official title** 2011 California Post-Installed Adhesive Anchors in Concrete Code
**Effective dates** January 1, 2011 – December 31, 2019
**Adopts with amendments** ACI 355.4-11, Qualification of Post-Installed Adhesive Anchors in Concrete and Commentary  
Read More: California Post-Installed Mechanical Anchors in Concrete Code 2019
California Residential Structural Concrete Code 2014
**Overview** The ACI 355.4-11 Standard for Qualification of Post-Installed Adhesive Anchors in Concrete provides comprehensive requirements for the testing, evaluation, and qualification of post-installed adhesive anchors in concrete. It includes guidelines for anchor performance, installation methods, and testing procedures to ensure the safety and reliability of adhesive anchors in concrete structures.
The 2011 California Post-Installed Adhesive Anchors in Concrete Code adopts the ACI 355.4-11 with specific amendments tailored to California’s unique conditions. These modifications address state-specific seismic considerations, environmental requirements, and compliance with regulations to ensure that post-installed adhesive anchors in California meet high standards of safety, performance, and reliability.
!mg author box
Maureen Guttman
AIA  
President  
Washington, DC

# California Low-rise Residential Fire Sprinkler Installation Code 2016
**Adoption Info of California Low-rise Residential Fire Sprinkler Installation Code 2016**
Discover more
Water
water
Fire Sprinkler
**Official title** 2016 California Low-rise Residential Fire Sprinkler Installation Code
**Effective dates** January 1, 2017 – December 31, 2019
**Adopts with amendments** NFPA 13R, 2016 Edition  
Read More: California Low-rise Residential Fire Sprinkler Installation Code 2022
California One- and Two-Family Dwelling Fire Sprinkler Installation Code 2016
**Overview** The NFPA 13R Standard for the Installation of Sprinkler Systems in Low-Rise Residential Occupancies provides comprehensive requirements for the design, installation, and maintenance of fire sprinkler systems in low-rise residential buildings to ensure effective fire protection and safety. It includes guidelines for sprinkler system components, installation methods, water supply requirements, and inspection, testing, and maintenance procedures.
The 2016 California Low-rise Residential Fire Sprinkler Installation Code adopts the NFPA 13R, 2016 Edition with specific amendments tailored to California’s unique conditions. These modifications address state-specific fire safety measures, seismic considerations, and compliance with environmental regulations to ensure that fire sprinkler systems in low-rise residential buildings in California meet high standards of safety, performance, and reliability.

# California Low-Alloy Steel Deformed and Plain Bars for Concrete Reinforcement Code 2016
**Adoption Info of California Low-Alloy Steel Deformed and Plain Bars for Concrete Reinforcement Code 2016**
Discover more
steel
Steel
Concrete
**Official title** 2016 California Low-Alloy Steel Deformed and Plain Bars for Concrete Reinforcement Code
**Effective dates** January 1, 2017 – December 31, 2019
**Published by** California Building Standards Commission (CBSC)  
Read More: California High-strength Low-alloy Piling with Atmospheric Corrosion Resistance for Use in Marine Environments Code, 2013 (2018)
California Steel Sheet, Zinc-Coated Galvanized or Zinc-Iron Alloy-Coated Galvannealed by the Hot-Dip Process Code, 2017
**Overview** The 2016 California Low-Alloy Steel Deformed and Plain Bars for Concrete Reinforcement Code provides comprehensive requirements for the material specifications, fabrication, and installation of low-alloy steel deformed and plain bars used for concrete reinforcement. It includes guidelines for chemical composition, mechanical properties, dimensions, bending, and placement to ensure the structural integrity and performance of reinforced concrete structures.
The 2016 edition incorporates updates and revisions to align with national standards such as ASTM A706/A706M. It is an essential reference for structural engineers, contractors, and code officials involved in the design and construction of reinforced concrete structures in California.
!mg author box

AIA

# California LP Gas Code 2020
**Adoption Info of California LP Gas Code 2020**
Discover more
Liquefied petroleum gas
NFPA 58, Liquefied Petroleum Gas Code: 2020 Edition
LP Gas
**Official title** 2020 California LP Gas Code
**Effective dates** January 1, 2021 – Present
**Adopts with amendments** NFPA 58, 2020 Edition  
Read More: California Compressed Gases and Cryogenic Fluids Code 2016
California Compressed Gases and Cryogenic Fluids Code 2020
**Overview** The NFPA 58 Standard for the Storage and Handling of Liquefied Petroleum Gases provides comprehensive requirements for the safe storage, handling, transportation, and use of liquefied petroleum gases (LP-Gas) to ensure the safety of personnel and property. It includes guidelines for system components, installation methods, safety measures, and inspection, testing, and maintenance procedures.
The 2020 California LP Gas Code adopts the NFPA 58, 2020 Edition with specific amendments tailored to California’s unique conditions. These modifications address state-specific safety measures, seismic considerations, and compliance with environmental regulations to ensure that the handling of LP-Gas in California meets high standards of safety, performance, and reliability.

# California Private Fire Service Main Installation Code 2019
**Adoption Info of California Private Fire Service Main Installation Code 2019**
**Official title** 2019 California Private Fire Service Main Installation Code
**Effective dates** January 1, 2020 – December 31, 2022
**Adopts with amendments** NFPA 24, 2019 Edition  
Read More: California Fire Pump Installation Code 2016
California Standpipe and Hose System Installation Code 2016
**Overview** The NFPA 24 Standard for the Installation of Private Fire Service Mains and Their Appurtenances provides comprehensive requirements for the design, installation, and maintenance of private fire service mains to ensure effective fire protection and safety. It includes guidelines for system components, installation methods, water supply requirements, and inspection, testing, and maintenance procedures.
The 2019 California Private Fire Service Main Installation Code adopts the NFPA 24, 2019 Edition with specific amendments tailored to California’s unique conditions. These modifications address state-specific fire safety measures, seismic considerations, and compliance with environmental regulations to ensure that private fire service mains in California meet high standards of safety, performance, and reliability.

# California Solder Joint Pressure Fitting Code for Cast Copper Alloy 2018
**Adoption Info of California Solder Joint Pressure Fitting Code for Cast Copper Alloy 2018**
**Official title** 2018 California Solder Joint Pressure Fitting Code for Cast Copper Alloy
**Effective dates** January 1, 2018 – December 31, 2020
**Adopts with amendments** ASME B16.18-2018, Cast Copper Alloy Solder Joint Pressure Fittings  
Read More: California Belt Manlift Code 2015
California Commercial HVAC Inspection and Maintenance Code 2012
**Overview** The ASME B16.18-2018 Standard for Cast Copper Alloy Solder Joint Pressure Fittings provides comprehensive requirements for the design, materials, dimensions, and testing of cast copper alloy pressure fittings used in piping systems. It includes guidelines for proper soldering techniques, pressure ratings, and inspection procedures to ensure the safety and reliability of the fittings.
The 2018 California Solder Joint Pressure Fitting Code for Cast Copper Alloy adopts the ASME B16.18-2018 with specific amendments tailored to California’s unique conditions. These modifications address state-specific safety measures, material considerations, and compliance with environmental regulations to ensure that solder joint pressure fittings in California meet high standards of safety, performance, and reliability.
!mg author box

# California Refrigeration System Safety Code 2016
**Adoption Info of California Refrigeration System Safety Code 2016**
**Official title** 2016 California Refrigeration System Safety Code
**Effective dates** January 1, 2017 – December 31, 2019
**Adopts with amendments** ANSI/ASHRAE 15-2013, Safety Standard for Refrigeration Systems  
Read More: California Clean Agent Fire Extinguishing Systems Code 2015
California Clean Agent Fire Extinguishing Systems Code 2018
**Overview** The ANSI/ASHRAE 15-2013 Safety Standard for Refrigeration Systems provides comprehensive requirements for the safe design, construction, installation, and operation of refrigeration systems. It includes guidelines for system components, refrigerant containment, pressure relief, and ventilation to ensure the safety of personnel and property.
The 2016 California Refrigeration System Safety Code adopts the ANSI/ASHRAE 15-2013 with specific amendments tailored to California’s unique conditions. These modifications address state-specific safety measures, seismic considerations, and compliance with environmental regulations to ensure that refrigeration systems in California meet high standards of safety, performance, and reliability.
!mg author box

AIA

# California Residential Code 2016
**Adoption Info of California Residential Code 2016**
**Official title** 2016 California Residential Code
**Effective dates** January 1, 2017 – December 31, 2019
**Adopts with amendments** International Residential Code 2015 (IRC 2015)  
Read More: California Residential Code 2019
California Residential Code 2022
**Overview** The International Residential Code (IRC) provides comprehensive requirements for the design, construction, and occupancy of one- and two-family dwellings and townhouses. It includes guidelines for structural integrity, energy efficiency, fire safety, plumbing, and mechanical systems to ensure the safety and performance of residential buildings.
The 2016 California Residential Code adopts the International Residential Code 2015 (IRC 2015) with specific amendments tailored to California’s unique conditions. These modifications address seismic design, energy efficiency, fire safety, and other state-specific requirements to ensure that residential buildings in California meet high standards of safety, performance, and reliability.

The 2012 California Solder Joint Pressure Fitting Code for Cast Copper Alloy adopts the ASME B16.18-2012 with specific amendments tailored to California’s unique conditions. # California Residential Structural Concrete Code 2014
**Adoption Info of California Residential Structural Concrete Code 2014**
**Official title** 2014 California Residential Structural Concrete Code
**Effective dates** January 1, 2014 – December 31, 2019
**Adopts with amendments** ACI 332-10, Residential Code Requirements for Structural Concrete  
Read More: California Residential Structural Concrete Code 2020  
California Concrete Thin Shells Code 2014
**Overview** The ACI 332-10 Residential Code Requirements for Structural Concrete provides comprehensive requirements for the design, construction, and materials of residential structural concrete. It includes guidelines for strength, durability, serviceability, and safety to ensure the integrity and performance of concrete in residential buildings.
The 2014 California Residential Structural Concrete Code adopts the ACI 332-10 with specific amendments tailored to California’s unique conditions. These modifications address state-specific seismic considerations, environmental requirements, and compliance with regulations to ensure that residential structural concrete in California meets high standards of safety, performance, and reliability.

## **Adoption Info of California Residential Code 2019**
**Official title** 2019 California Residential Code
**Effective dates** January 1, 2020 – December 31, 2022
**Adopts with amendments** International Residential Code 2018 (IRC 2018)  
Read More: California Residential Code 2022
California Building Code 2013 (Vol 1 & 2)
**Overview** The International Residential Code (IRC) provides comprehensive requirements for the design, construction, and occupancy of one- and two-family dwellings and townhouses. It includes guidelines for structural integrity, energy efficiency, fire safety, plumbing, and mechanical systems to ensure the safety and performance of residential buildings.
The 2019 California Residential Code adopts the International Residential Code 2018 (IRC 2018) with specific amendments tailored to California’s unique conditions. These modifications address seismic design, energy efficiency, fire safety, and other state-specific requirements to ensure that residential buildings in California meet high standards of safety, performance, and reliability.

# California Process Piping Code 2020
**Adoption Info of California Process Piping Code 2020**
**Official title** 2020 California Process Piping Code
**Effective dates** January 1, 2021 – Present
**Adopts with amendments** ASME B31.3-2020, Process Piping
Read More: California Conveyor and Related Equipment Code 2015
California Conveyor and Related Equipment Code 2018
**Overview** The ASME B31.3-2020 Process Piping Standard provides comprehensive requirements for the design, materials, fabrication, testing, inspection, and maintenance of process piping systems. It includes guidelines for pressure ratings, welding, fittings, supports, and safety measures to ensure the integrity and reliability of piping systems used in chemical, petroleum, pharmaceutical, and other processing plants.
The 2020 California Process Piping Code adopts the ASME B31.3-2020 with specific amendments tailored to California’s unique conditions. These modifications address state-specific safety measures, environmental considerations, and compliance with regulations to ensure that process piping systems in California meet high standards of safety, performance, and reliability.

**Adoption Info of California Refrigeration System Safety Code 2013**
Discover more
Fire Extinguishing
Fire extinguisher
**Official title** 2013 California Refrigeration System Safety Code
**Effective dates** January 1, 2014 – December 31, 2016
**Adopts with amendments** ANSI/ASHRAE 15-2010, Safety Standard for Refrigeration Systems  
Read More: California Refrigeration System Safety Code 2016
California Clean Agent Fire Extinguishing Systems Code 2015
**Overview** The ANSI/ASHRAE 15-2010 Safety Standard for Refrigeration Systems provides comprehensive requirements for the safe design, construction, installation, and operation of refrigeration systems. It includes guidelines for system components, refrigerant containment, pressure relief, and ventilation to ensure the safety of personnel and property.
The 2013 California Refrigeration System Safety Code adopts the ANSI/ASHRAE 15-2010 with specific amendments tailored to California’s unique conditions. These modifications address state-specific safety measures, seismic considerations, and compliance with environmental regulations to ensure that refrigeration systems in California meet high standards of safety, performance, and reliability.

California Concrete Thin Shells Code 2019
Discover more
Building material
concrete
Concrete
**Overview** The ACI 332-14 Residential Code Requirements for Structural Concrete provides comprehensive requirements for the design, construction, and materials of residential structural concrete. The 2020 California Residential Structural Concrete Code adopts the ACI 332-14 with specific amendments tailored to California’s unique conditions. These modifications address state-specific seismic considerations, environmental requirements, and compliance with regulations to ensure that residential structural concrete in California meets high standards of safety, performance, and reliability.

# California Standpipe and Hose System Installation Code 2016
**Adoption Info of California Standpipe and Hose System Installation Code 2016**
**Official title** 2016 California Standpipe and Hose System Installation Code
**Effective dates** January 1, 2017 – December 31, 2019
**Adopts with amendments** NFPA 14, 2016 Edition  
Read More: California Low-rise Residential Fire Sprinkler Installation Code 2016
California Low-rise Residential Fire Sprinkler Installation Code 2022
**Overview** The NFPA 14 Standard for the Installation of Standpipe and Hose Systems provides comprehensive requirements for the design, installation, and maintenance of standpipe and hose systems to ensure effective fire protection and safety. It includes guidelines for system components, installation methods, water supply requirements, and inspection, testing, and maintenance procedures.
The 2016 California Standpipe and Hose System Installation Code adopts the NFPA 14, 2016 Edition with specific amendments tailored to California’s unique conditions. These modifications address state-specific fire safety measures, seismic considerations, and compliance with environmental regulations to ensure that standpipe and hose systems in California meet high standards of safety, performance, and reliability.

# California Storm Shelter Code 2014
**Adoption Info of California Storm Shelter Code 2014**
**Official title** 2014 California Storm Shelter Code
**Effective dates** January 1, 2014 – December 31, 2020
**Adopts with amendments** ICC 500-2008 Standard for the Design and Construction of Storm Shelters  
Read More: California Storm Shelter Code 2020
California Standard on the Design and Construction of Log Structures 2017
**Overview** The ICC 500-2008 Standard for the Design and Construction of Storm Shelters provides comprehensive requirements for the design, construction, and inspection of storm shelters to ensure their safety and reliability during extreme weather events. It includes guidelines for structural design, impact resistance, ventilation, and emergency management to protect the occupants during storms and tornadoes.
The 2014 California Storm Shelter Code adopts the ICC 500-2008 with specific amendments tailored to California’s unique conditions. These modifications address additional safety measures, structural integrity, and compliance with state-specific requirements for storm shelters to ensure that they meet high standards of safety, performance, and reliability in California.

# California Typical Timber Construction Details Code 2003
**Adoption Info of California Typical Timber Construction Details Code 2003**
**Official title** 2003 California Typical Timber Construction Details Code
**Effective dates** January 1, 2003 – December 31, 2013
**Published by** California Building Standards Commission (CBSC)  
Read More: California ABA Standards 2015
California Historical Building Code 2022
Discover more
Timber
Lumber
timber
**Overview** The 2003 California Typical Timber Construction Details Code provides comprehensive requirements and standard details for timber construction in residential and nonresidential buildings. It includes guidelines for framing, connections, spans, and other construction details to ensure the structural integrity and safety of timber structures. The code covers typical timber construction practices, ensuring that buildings meet California’s standards for safety, durability, and performance.
The 2003 edition incorporates best practices and standard construction details prevalent at the time, providing a valuable reference for architects, engineers, builders, and code officials involved in timber construction in California.

# California Steel Sheet, Zinc-5 Percent, Aluminum Alloy-Coated by the Hot-Dip Process Code 2013
**Adoption Info of California Steel Sheet, Zinc-5 Percent, Aluminum Alloy-Coated by the Hot-Dip Process Code 2013**
**Official title** 2013 California Steel Sheet, Zinc-5 Percent, Aluminum Alloy-Coated by the Hot-Dip Process Code
**Effective dates** January 1, 2013 – December 31, 2016
**Published by** California Building Standards Commission (CBSC)  
Read More: California High-strength Steel Bars for Prestressed Concrete Code 2018
[California Low-Alloy Steel Deformed and Plain Bars for Concrete Reinforcement Code 2016](https://bcapcodes.org/california/low-alloy-steel-deformed-plain-bars-for-concrete-reinforcement2016/)
**Overview** The 2013 California Steel Sheet, Zinc-5 Percent, Aluminum Alloy-Coated by the Hot-Dip Process Code provides comprehensive requirements for the specifications, manufacturing, and quality control of steel sheets coated with a zinc-5 percent aluminum alloy through the hot-dip process. It includes guidelines for coating thickness, adhesion, corrosion resistance, and mechanical properties to ensure the durability and performance of alloy-coated steel sheets used in construction.
The 2013 edition incorporates updates and revisions to align with national standards such as ASTM A875/A875M. It is an essential reference for manufacturers, architects, engineers, and code officials involved in the selection and use of zinc-5 percent aluminum alloy-coated steel sheets in construction projects in California.
!mg author box
Maureen Guttman
AIA  
President  
Washington, DC

# California Welded and Seamless Steel Pipe Piles Code, 2010 (R2018)
**Adoption Info of California Welded and Seamless Steel Pipe Piles Code 2010 (R2018)**
Discover more
steel
Plain Carbon-Steel
Carbon steel
**Official title** 2010 California Welded and Seamless Steel Pipe Piles Code (Revised 2018)
**Effective dates** January 1, 2010 – December 31, 2019
**Published by** California Building Standards Commission (CBSC)  
Read More: California Carbon Structural Steel Code, 2014
California Phenolic Duct Construction Code 2015
**Overview** The 2010 California Welded and Seamless Steel Pipe Piles Code (Revised 2018) provides comprehensive requirements for the design, fabrication, installation, and inspection of welded and seamless steel pipe piles used in foundation construction. It includes guidelines for material specifications, welding standards, installation methods, and quality control measures to ensure the structural integrity, performance, and durability of steel pipe piles.
The 2018 revision incorporates updates and revisions to reflect advancements in steel pipe pile technology and aligns with national standards such as ASTM and AISC. It is an essential reference for structural engineers, contractors, and code officials involved in the design and construction of foundations using steel pipe piles in California.

# California Structural Glued Laminated Timber Dimensions Code 2010
**Adoption Info of California Structural Glued Laminated Timber Dimensions Code 2010**
Discover more
Timber
Lumber
timber
**Official title** 2010 California Structural Glued Laminated Timber Dimensions Code
**Effective dates** January 1, 2010 – December 31, 2016
**Published by** California Building Standards Commission (CBSC)  
Read More: California Structural Glued Laminated Timber Appearance Grades Code 2001
California Typical Timber Construction Details Code 2003
**Overview** The 2010 California Structural Glued Laminated Timber Dimensions Code provides comprehensive requirements for the dimensions and size tolerances of structural glued laminated timber (glulam). It includes guidelines for manufacturing standards, dimensional tolerances, and quality control measures to ensure the structural integrity and performance of glulam timber used in construction.
The 2010 edition incorporates best practices and standards for glulam dimensions prevalent at the time, providing a valuable reference for architects, engineers, builders, and code officials involved in the design and construction of structures using glulam timber in California.

# California Structural Glued Laminated Timber Appearance Grades Code 2001
**Adoption Info of California Structural Glued Laminated Timber Appearance Grades Code 2001**
**Official title** 2001 California Structural Glued Laminated Timber Appearance Grades Code
**Effective dates** January 1, 2001 – December 31, 2010
**Published by** California Building Standards Commission (CBSC)  
Read More: California Typical Timber Construction Details Code 2003
California ABA Standards 2015
**Overview** The 2001 California Structural Glued Laminated Timber Appearance Grades Code provides comprehensive requirements for the appearance grades of structural glued laminated timber (glulam). It includes guidelines for grading criteria, visual inspection standards, and classification of appearance grades to ensure the aesthetic quality and structural performance of glulam timber used in construction.
The 2001 edition incorporates best practices and standards for glulam appearance grading prevalent at the time, providing a valuable reference for architects, engineers, builders, and code officials involved in the selection and use of glulam timber in California.
!mg author box
Maureen Guttman
AIA  
President

# California Stationary Fuel Cell Power Code 2015
**Adoption Info of California Stationary Fuel Cell Power Code 2015**
**Official title** 2015 California Stationary Fuel Cell Power Code
**Effective dates** January 1, 2015 – December 31, 2019
**Adopts with amendments** NFPA 853, 2015 Edition  
Read More: California Stationary Fuel Cell Power Code 2020
California Fire Wall Code 2015
**Overview** The NFPA 853 Standard for the Installation of Stationary Fuel Cell Power Systems provides comprehensive requirements for the design, installation, and maintenance of stationary fuel cell power systems to ensure safety, reliability, and performance. It includes guidelines for system components, installation methods, ventilation, fuel supply, and inspection, testing, and maintenance procedures.
The 2015 California Stationary Fuel Cell Power Code adopts the NFPA 853, 2015 Edition with specific amendments tailored to California’s unique conditions. These modifications address state-specific safety measures, seismic considerations, and compliance with environmental regulations to ensure that stationary fuel cell power systems in California meet high standards of safety, performance, and reliability.
!mg author box
Maureen Guttman
AIA  
President  
Washington, DC

# California Steel Sheet, Zinc-Coated Galvanized or Zinc-Iron Alloy-Coated Galvannealed by the Hot-Dip Process Code, 2017
**Adoption Info of California Steel Sheet, Zinc-Coated Galvanized or Zinc-Iron Alloy-Coated Galvannealed by the Hot-Dip Process Code 2017**
Discover more
Carbon steel
steel
zinc
**Official title** 2017 California Steel Sheet, Zinc-Coated Galvanized or Zinc-Iron Alloy-Coated Galvannealed by the Hot-Dip Process Code
**Effective dates** January 1, 2017 – December 31, 2019
**Published by** California Building Standards Commission (CBSC)  
Read More: [California Deformed and Plain Carbon-steel Bars for Concrete Reinforcement Code 2015ae1](https://bcapcodes.org/california/deformed-plain-carbon-steel-bars-for-concrete-reinforcement-code-2015/)
California Welded and Seamless Steel Pipe Piles Code, 2010 (R2018)
**Overview** The 2017 California Steel Sheet, Zinc-Coated Galvanized or Zinc-Iron Alloy-Coated Galvannealed by the Hot-Dip Process Code provides comprehensive requirements for the specifications, manufacturing, and quality control of steel sheets coated with zinc or zinc-iron alloy through the hot-dip process. It includes guidelines for coating thickness, adhesion, corrosion resistance, and mechanical properties to ensure the durability and performance of coated steel sheets used in construction.
The 2017 edition incorporates updates and revisions to align with national standards such as ASTM A653/A653M and ASTM A924/A924M. It is an essential reference for manufacturers, architects, engineers, and code officials involved in the selection and use of galvanized or galvannealed steel sheets in construction projects in California.
!mg author box

AIA

# Arkansas Current Building Codes
Arkansas building codes play a pivotal role in ensuring the safety and integrity of construction projects within the state. These regulations encompass a wide range of factors, including structural integrity, electrical systems, plumbing, and more. Staying informed and compliant with Arkansas building codes is essential for builders and property owners to guarantee the well-being of their structures and occupants.
!Arkansas building codes
Current Commercial Code of Arkansas
_Arkansas Energy Code for New Building Construction with 2014 Arkansas Supplements and Amendments_  
Based on the 2009 IECC; Chapter 5 of the 2009 IECC allows for an alternative compliance pathway for commercial structures through ASHRAE Standard 90.1-2007.

#### Arkansas Residential Code 2021
